# Evidence Expansion Pass — Chapters 29–35 — Pass 001

**Artifact scope:** Chapters 29–35 only  
**Evidence cutoff:** 2026-07-19 EDT  
**Governing controls:** `PRODUCTION_EVIDENCE_POLICY.md`; `EVIDENCE_IMPROVEMENT_QUEUE.md`; controlling chapter claim maps; Historical Evidence Review standard  
**Mutation boundary:** report only. No draft, upstream research, claim map, evidence queue, architecture, assembly, or review record was edited.

## Executive decision

- **Claim-ID parity:** 190/190 queue IDs accounted for: Chapter 29 (26), Chapter 30 (23), Chapter 31 (28), Chapter 32 (27), Chapter 33 (30), Chapter 34 (27), Chapter 35 (29).
- **Recommendations:** **KEEP 190 / REWRITE 0 / DEFER 0 / REMOVE 0.** “KEEP” means the present bounded wording remains supportable; it does not mean the open research question is resolved.
- **Material strengthening:** no inspected new source supports stronger draft language in this pass. Existing primary/official sources continue to support the bounded claims and their explicit limits.
- **Priority blockers:** Chapter 29 still lacks an inspectable NCSML decision log/minute/directive allocating a distinct June authorization to Gail Naughton; Chapter 32’s SEC filings establish domain structure but not ADM approval authority; Chapter 33’s official award releases establish customer selection and announced program/site context but not proposal, product, capital, or site authority.
- **Chapter 35 B1:** **NOT RESOLVED.** Current first-party company pages show a live family-branded business, fundraising infrastructure, and a wholesale customer path; a dated March 16, 2023 CBJ article identifies Sydney as Almost Famous co-owner and Goldman Sachs 10,000 Small Businesses alumna and quotes her SBA advocacy. None allocates authorship of the fundraising/wholesale pathway to Sydney, verifies a current 2026 office, identifies the concrete downside she accepted in going full-time, or proves a usable opening she personally made for another builder. The smallest intervention is one recorded, decision-specific Sydney interview plus one corroborating operational record naming the beneficiary/pathway and co-actors.

## Discovery record and source-boundary decisions

### Chapter 35 priority discovery

1. **Current/datestamped role:** The current Almost Famous “Our Story” page, inspected 2026-07-19, names Sydney, Robyn, Bill, and Carter and describes a family enterprise; it does **not** name officers or current roles. The same-day site showed an operating Cedar Rapids retail address and store hours, but business operation is not proof that Sydney remains CEO/co-owner. The latest inspected role-specific source remains the March 16, 2023 Corridor Business Journal article, which identifies Sydney as co-owner; the February 6, 2023 Senate and KCRG sources identify her as CEO/co-founder. **Current 2026 role remains unresolved.**
2. **Accepted downside for the full-time choice:** No inspected government, company, or full-text news source identifies the prior job, compensation, school plan, debt, guarantee, savings, ownership stake, foregone offer, or household consequence behind “making the leap.” **Accepted downside remains unresolved.**
3. **Concrete usable opening/handoff:** The company’s current first-party fundraising page offers organizations custom online sales, local pickup/delivery coordination, and nationwide box shipping; its wholesale page offers retailers customer service, custom product/labeling, and an inquiry route. These are concrete company-level pathways, but neither page names Sydney as author/approver or identifies a beneficiary outcome. The 2023 CBJ article documents her small-business-policy advocacy and program alumni status, not a completed opening she personally delivered. **No Sydney-authored handoff is established.**
4. **Family co-agency:** The company’s current story continues collective family grammar and names all four Rieckhoffs. This corroborates the need to preserve family coagency but does not allocate current authority.
5. **B1 smallest intervention:** Obtain (a) a recorded interview in which Sydney identifies one specific training, job, supplier/customer, financing, mentorship, or space pathway she personally initiated or approved, when and why; (b) one contemporaneous corroborating artifact—agreement, program roster, hire/training record, wholesale onboarding record, financing referral, signed partnership record, or named beneficiary testimony; and (c) the exact co-actors and beneficiary consequence. This single paired intervention can test current role, downside, and authored handoff without redesigning the chapter. If it fails, B1 remains and final-manuscript PASS should remain withheld.

### Chapters 29, 32, and 33 authority searches

- **Chapter 29:** Internet Archive captures continue to prove Naughton’s dated public commitment and plural board/staff activity, not a decision log. The smallest unresolved record class is June 2008 NCSML board/emergency minutes, incident-command logs, email directives, insurer/FEMA submissions, or a decision-specific interview allocating one authorization and immediate consequence.
- **Chapter 32:** ADM’s 2020 SEC exhibit, 10-Q, and 10-K establish business-unit/officer scope and a distributed segment structure. They do not disclose who proposed or approved Cedar Rapids idling, product routing, or furloughs. The smallest intervention is an April 2020 delegation-of-authority record, plant directive, furlough authorization, or attributable testimony naming the approving actor and threshold.
- **Chapter 33:** Official RTX/Collins releases establish the awards, values, announced work locations, products, and public executive voices. They do not allocate capture, bid, product, pricing, capital, site, staffing, or program authority. The smallest intervention is one approved bid/gate record or decision-specific interview paired with a Cedar Rapids work-allocation record.

### Chapters 30, 31, and 34 citation-strengthening result

- **Chapter 30:** Official NCSML retrospective support remains usable for tenure, campaign scale, building movement, expansion, and reopening, but original conservation, engineering, board, campaign, and construction records are still needed for transaction-level strengthening. No conflicting measurement was silently harmonized.
- **Chapter 31:** Contemporaneous CBJ support remains strong for the 2010 site request, plan, funding sequence, council concerns, Project for Public Spaces role, and opening-period details. Council packets/minutes, the property instrument, bylaws, consultant contract, and merchant agreements remain the smallest primary-source set.
- **Chapter 34:** Contemporaneous local reporting with direct Winker quotations remains sufficient for the bounded opening, damage, risk acknowledgment, and host-kitchen continuation. Permits, inspection/damage records, host agreements, exact opening records, and final-disposition records remain needed; no long-term recovery claim was strengthened.

## Claim-by-claim accounting

## Chapter 29: Thirty-One Feet

### EIQ-29-C01
- **Claim (exact controlling-map statement):** “the next chapter receives the obligation to keep a mission and its holdings accessible when a building fails. In June 2008, that obligation reached the National Czech & Slovak Museum & Library before anyone there could count the damage. While NCSML remained inaccessible and its losses could not be counted, Gail Naughton publicly committed the institution to continue preserving Czech and Slovak heritage and to rebuild; the removal of two semi-truck loads and emergency planning remained collective board-and-staff work, not her proved authorization.”
- **Where it appears:** Body paragraph 1.
- **Current sources and type:** `production_runs/Production_Run_001/research/chapter-29-gail-naughton-flood-v002.md`, “Essential Supported Facts,” “Responsible Narrative Spine,” “Supported Interpretation,” and “Inheritance”; `production_runs/Production_Run_001/character_briefs/gail-naughton-v002.md`, “Defining Decision,” “Evidence Boundary,” and “Closing Handoff”; `production_runs/Production_Run_001/narrative_discovery/ndr-chapter-29-gail-naughton-flood.md`, “The One Unforgettable Truth,” “Evidence Boundary and Confidence,” and “Frozen Inheritance”; `production_runs/Production_Run_001/chapter_intents/chapter-29-gail-naughton-flood.md`, “Historical Material Required,” “Historical Material To Avoid,” and “Transition.” Source-type audit: The map cites qualified Research plus Character Brief/NDR/Intent. The Research rests on two dated NCSML statements recovered in Internet Archive captures (institutional primary/public statements), a contemporaneous NCSML news index (institutional primary index), and NPR reporting allocating later curator/volunteer work (contemporaneous journalism). Character Brief/NDR/Intent are bounded syntheses or narrative controls, not independent historical corroboration.
- **Support limit:** Naughton is the attributable public voice, not a proved emergency authorizer. “We,” board, staff, curator, and volunteers retain their own agency; later Chapter 30 recovery cannot prove June authority. EIQ-29-01 — recover a distinct Naughton emergency authorization, its scope, alternative, and immediate consequence. For this claim specifically, inspect source records that allocate the actors, timing, authority, exposure, and consequence described here; until then retain the draft’s present bounded wording.
- **Confidence:** High for dated public words, office, inaccessibility, collective removal/planning, and transition; moderate-high for bounded leadership interpretation.
- **Historical importance:** High — this material claim defines the June 2008 commitment-before-inventory story, preserves plural emergency agency, or protects the Chapter 29/30 boundary.
- **Recommendation:** **KEEP** — retain the present bounded wording and qualification; the pass found no inspectable evidence warranting stronger prose.

### EIQ-29-C02
- **Claim (exact controlling-map statement):** “Naughton was the museum's president and chief executive officer, and the June 14 statement was attributed to her. Her office could carry a promise; it could not turn work performed by “we” into an operation she alone ordered. Two semi-truck loads had been removed before people were told to leave, and board and staff were holding emergency meetings, but the surviving account does not allocate object selection, loading, evacuation, spending, or meeting authority to Naughton.”

### EIQ-29-C04
- **Claim (exact controlling-map statement):** “The scale matters because access was gone and damage unknown while organizations across Cedar Rapids competed for safety, information, labor, temporary space, and attention. On June 14, the museum's immediate problem was not yet a campaign, a building move, an addition, or reopening. It was what an executive could responsibly promise before inspection and without sole command. A statement limited to access and safety would have been structurally safer, although no source says Naughton considered that alternative. Her documented choice was to speak beyond an inventory that did not yet exist.”

### EIQ-32-C01
- **Claim (exact controlling-map statement):** “shared place, gathered traffic, selection, utilities, programming, and smaller spaces allow entrepreneurs to test products without first carrying a whole storefront. At industrial scale, however, the owner controls the platform. In April 2020, ADM temporarily idled Cedar Rapids dry-mill ethanol production, redirected parts of its processing response toward other products, and announced about ninety local furloughs; Chris Cuddy, leader of the relevant business domain, publicly called the actions difficult without claiming personal approval.”

## Chapter 33: Aerospace After Collins

### EIQ-33-C01
- **Claim (exact controlling-map statement):** “Cedar Rapids retains adaptable industrial capability but not demonstrated final local control over its use. In January 2026, RTX announced from Cedar Rapids a $438 million FAA Radar System Replacement award, with Nathan “Nate” Boelkins speaking as president of Collins Aerospace's Avionics business. In 2025 and 2026, Collins Aerospace/RTX received an $80 million Black Hawk avionics award and a $438 million FAA radar award connected to Cedar Rapids; Nathan Boelkins and Jenny Miller supplied leadership voices, but the record identifies no personal bid, product, capital, site, or staffing authorization.”
- **Where it appears:** Body paragraph 1.
- **Current sources and type:** `production_runs/Production_Run_001/research/chapter-33-aerospace-after-collins-v002.md`, “Essential Supported Facts,” “Responsible Narrative Spine,” “Supported Interpretation,” and “Inheritance”; `production_runs/Production_Run_001/character_briefs/nathan-boelkins.md`, “Defining Decision,” “Evidence Boundary,” and “Closing Handoff”; `production_runs/Production_Run_001/narrative_discovery/ndr-chapter-33-aerospace-after-collins.md`, “The One Unforgettable Truth,” “Evidence Boundary and Confidence,” and “Frozen Inheritance”; `production_runs/Production_Run_001/chapter_intents/chapter-33-aerospace-after-collins.md`, “Historical Material Required,” “Historical Material To Avoid,” and “Transition.” Source-type audit: The map cites qualified Research plus Character Brief/NDR/Intent.
